  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/185309405" />
    <a title="Lea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5152540-lea"><img alt="Lea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341265725p2/5152540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/185309405?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lea" href="/user/show/5152540-lea">Lea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385739184" href="/book/show/12681104-rapture">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer185309405&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer185309405" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16939023823611069161"><i>
  <b>In Dedication to the end of the Fallen Series by Lauren Kate....</b>
</i><br/><br/>Because I have an incredibly immature sense of humor and wanted to show off my mad skills at photo editing, I created this Ermagerd meme. Enjoy.<br/><br/><div>
  <br/>
  <b>
    <b>
      
        <a href='http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-bEpZHpYjcZE/UL_i9nH8CtI/AAAAAAAAD-g/xZrDMReJ_Qc/s1600/Fallen.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
          <img height='400' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380353228i/706623.jpg' width='245' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
        </a>
      
    </b>
  </b>
</div><br/><br/><br/>Ermahgerd!!<br/><br/><br/>Ok. Let's get serious here.<br/><br/><br/><b>LC's Take:</b><br/><br/>And now...<br/><br/>The epic conclusion to the <i>Fallen</i> series by Lauren Kate.<br/><br/>And by epic, I mean the following:<br/><br/>1.) Totally ridiculous<br/>2.) Painfully cliche<br/>3.) LOL hilarious for all the wrong</span>
  <span id="freeText16939023823611069161" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>In Dedication to the end of the Fallen Series by Lauren Kate....</b>
</i><br><br>Because I have an incredibly immature sense of humor and wanted to show off my mad skills at photo editing, I created this Ermagerd meme. Enjoy.<br><br><div>
  <br>
  <b>
    <b>
      
        <a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-bEpZHpYjcZE/UL_i9nH8CtI/AAAAAAAAD-g/xZrDMReJ_Qc/s1600/Fallen.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
          <img height="400" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380353228i/706623.jpg" width="245" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
        </a>
      
    </b>
  </b>
</div><br><br><br>Ermahgerd!!<br><br><br>Ok. Let's get serious here.<br><br><br><b>LC's Take:</b><br><br>And now...<br><br>The epic conclusion to the <i>Fallen</i> series by Lauren Kate.<br><br>And by epic, I mean the following:<br><br>1.) Totally ridiculous<br>2.) Painfully cliche<br>3.) LOL hilarious for all the wrong reasons<br>4.) Convoluted beyond all human reasoning<br>5.) Inexplicably addicting in a *slightly* unsettling yet delightful kind of way<br><br>Yep, it's been a looooooong time coming for this one guys. <i>Fallen</i> was the first book I ever read and reviewed on <i>LC's Adventures in Libraryland</i> so you might say I have a bit of a soft spot for it-- but that doesn't mean I won't respectfully rip it to shreds where needs be. <br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-2M02y2ud-Cw/UL_Y4f_jn_I/AAAAAAAAD-A/rfc6l2b1RRA/s1600/555.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="300" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380353228i/706624.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>So let's jump right in. Now, after three ranting reviews for the previous 3 books where I gripe at length about this series, a lot of you are probably wondering why the heck I even bothered with the last one. Well, my relationship with <i>Fallen</i> is complicated. I love it and hate it at the same time. The main characters are beyond aggravating, the dialogue is so cheesy you have to wonder what planet they're from where people <i>actually</i> talk like that, the romance is completely dysfunctional, and I lost track of the plot about 800 pages ago.<br><br>So. My reasons for reading this book?<br><br>A.) Figure out what the flying fig newton all of this has been leading up to<br><br>B.) See if Luce becomes less of a brain-dead idiot and Daniel becomes less of an ass-hat, and<br><br>C.) Find out if the entire series could be redeemed by some miracle in the last installment.<br><br><b>~Brief Summary~</b><br><br>I'm going to try and not give away any spoilers for those of you who are just dying to read this series or haven't finished it yet, but here is the gist of things: Luce and Daniel have been falling in love, over and over again in every lifetime, for thousands of years. Daniel is a fallen angel and Luce is just a normal girl-- except for the fact that in every lifetime she ends up bursting into flames the minute Daniel and she kiss. Bummer, right? So in the last book, Luce went back in time through a bunch of her past lives to figure out why she and Daniel are cursed and try to fix things. Along the way, she met this little gargoyle named "Bill" who was shady as f*** and who turned out to be the devil in disguise [Note: This really wasn't that big of a surprise-- it was actually pretty predictable-- so I don't feel bad about giving that much away]. And now good ol' Lucifer has plans to basically wipe out the last 7,000 years of human history because Luce didn't destroy her soul at the end of Book 3. (Why does the Father-of-All-Evil have it out against Luce and Daniel? Beats the crap out of me-- none of this was explained until about the last half of the final book...) So, in <i>Rapture</i>,  Luce, Daniel, and their other angel friends have NINE DAYS to find out where the original Fall of angels took place when God threw them out of Heaven, effectively stopping Lucifer from carrying out his diabolical plans to destroy life as we know it.<br><br>Confused yet? Join the club. <br><br><b>~Three Things I Liked (sort of)~ </b><br><br>So first off, I have to say, there were aspects to <i>Rapture</i> that pleasantly surprised me; even <i>impressed</i> me in how well they were done--you know, compared to the craptastic first three books. So let's start off with the positives:<br><br><b>1.)</b>The descriptive language was good. Like, <i>really</i> good. For all the ick I find in these books, I have to hand it to LK, she is pretty talented when it comes to providing readers with rich, vivid descriptions of the scenes playing out-- and <i>Rapture</i> more than any other book in this series is a testament to her ability to do this. Kudos on the scene-setting Lauren, it really was beautiful.<br><br><b>2.)</b>There was FINALLY a sense of urgency in the plot that was completely missing from the last three books. <i>Fallen, Torment</i>, and <i>Passion</i> were not only painfully slow but they seemed to be going absolutely nowhere. By the end of the third book, I was so flipping confused I had a headache. But <i>Rapture</i> managed to capture my attention because it had a direction-- <i>things happened and things were explained</i>. Was it a water-tight plot? Not so much, but thank the Good Lawd Almighty, there was at least <i>action</i>!<br><br><b>3.)</b> I can't rave <i>too</i> much about this because it was only a slight improvement, but both Daniel and Luce were *marginally* more likable in this book than in any of the previous ones. What I could NOT stand about these books was the totally unbelievable and dysfunctional relationship between Luce, the desperately-clingy and dumb-as-a-rock female character, and Daniel, the chauvinistic jerk-wad who constantly belittles and pushes her around. This was ever-so-minutely improved in this book, BUT I still have plenty to say about how sucky the two of them are overall, so stay tuned. <br><br>OK so those are the good things about <i>Rapture</i>-- three things that resulted in my three-star rating. Now onto the fun part!<br><br><b>~Ten Things That Sucked~</b><br><br>So what didn't I like about <i>Rapture</i>? I've already elaborated at length about the many aspects of this series that made me want to knock my head against a wall-- repeatedly-- so I'll spare you and say that if you're really that interested, go check out my past three reviews. But more specific to <i>this</i> book and how the entire series wrapped up, here are my thoughts on the parts that seriously blew:<br><br><b>1.)</b>According to this story, Luce and Daniel's love is <i>the</i> most epic, mind-blowing, knock-your-socks-off love ever to exist. The very beginning of good and evil all originated because of their love. The fate of Earth and all human history basically comes down to them. BUT FOR THE LOVE OF GOD <i>WHY???</i> I <i>still</i> have no idea. <i>WHY</i> is the love between Luce and Daniel so stinking profound that everyone and everything hangs in the balance because of it, and legions of angels are willing to fight and die over it? There is absolutely NOTHING exceptional about either Luce or Daniel-- they are in fact pretty darned boring-- and their relationship is beyond mundane. In the <i>entire length</i> of this series, not ONCE have I found anything remotely grand or real about Luce and Daniel's "love." Not once did I go, "Aww they're so cute!" or "Shucks, I hope I find someone that dreamy." On the contrary, they're both hopelessly self-absorbed and their relationship is at the best of times awkward, bland and generic, and at the worst of times abusive, dysfunctional, and in dire need of Dr. Phil.<br><br><b>2.)</b>Luce was the same pathetically useless, boring, and wimpy lump of oatmeal that she has been throughout the whole series-- I could see where LK was trying for some character development in this last book where Luce finally gained a backbone-- but honestly it just didn't happen. There were parts in this book where Luce was <i>so</i> freaking pathetic that I wanted to slap her across the face and scream, "<i>What is WRONG with you?!</i>" Here are some examples that nearly sent me up in flames of rage:<br><br><b>SCENE #1:</b> Luce and Daniel are going after one of the ancient relics they need to find out the location of the Fall from Heaven, and Luce has to swim under water to get to it because it's in a sunken cathedral. Well Daniel can't go into the cathedral because it's sacred ground and he's a fallen angel, so he stands guard outside of it to make sure Luce is OK. But THEN he swims away and just leaves her there. <i>Sh-yeah!  LEAVES HER THERE UNDER WATER IN A FLIPPING CATHEDRAL TO DROWN. </i>So Luce-- the girl Daniel supposedly would risk Heaven and Earth for-- <i>nearly dies</i> because Ass-hat Daniel abandons her. And when she makes it back up to the surface and tries to ask where the heck he went, this is how it goes down:<br><br><i>"What happened to you?" [Luce] cried. "I almost--"<br><br>"Luce," he [Daniel] warned. "shhh." <br><br>~p.91</i><br><br>Whoa, whoa, hold the phone. Are you <i>freaking kidding me?</i> The girl is trying to find out why her boyfriend almost let her drown and he's telling her to "shhhh"?!?<br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-fnd_xCIwxnE/UL_XPKYSiKI/AAAAAAAAD94/P55Nh7PedFo/s1600/31351448.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="300" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380351230i/704916.jpg" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I'm pretty sure that makes him the biggest butt-face known to man, but of course, Luce being Luce, she let's it slide and doesn't seem to be at all miffed by the fact that Daniel abandoned her underwater to fend for herself and almost <i>die</i>. No biggie right? <br><br><b>SCENE #2:</b> Near the end of the book, Cam (who happens to be one of the only likable characters in this series) goes to talk to Luce and sort of smooth over their rocky past. BUT all Luce can do is practically have a brain aneurysm because she's freaked that Daniel is going to see another guy talking to her. <i>Heaven flipping forbid.</i><br><br><i>"She wanted to leave. What if Daniel looked over and saw her in this dim cave with Cam? They were arguing, but Daniel wouldn't be able to tell that from a distance. What did they look like, she and Cam?"<br><br>~p.319</i><br><br>Well, Luce, I think a better question you should be asking yourself is: <i>"Who the hell cares?"</i> And even <i>more</i> to the point, if your relationship with your boyfriend is so unstable that he doesn't even trust you to talk to another guy without freaking out and getting all suspicious, and <i>you</i> can't leave the leash he's got you on for 5 minutes-- isn't that like a warning sign that maybe, just mayyybeeee, there's a problem? <br><br>Now, let me make this clear-- there was <i>nothing</i> shady going on between Luce and Cam, this was a totally platonic conversation they're having-- and Luce is scared to death that her psycho-jealous angel bf is going to flip a crap if he sees her with Cam. There's something majorly wrong with this, no?<br><br><b>SCENE #3:</b> This was my favorite-- I was reading this and just wanted to set the book down and start a slow-clap for Luce after this:<br><br><i>"Now, tell me who you are." [Daniel speaking]<br><br>"Well... I'm Lucinda Price. I'm the girl you fell in love with."<br><br>Daniel's violet eyes filled with tears. He whispered: "More."<br><br>"Isn't that enough?"<br><br>~p.327 </i><br><br>Really Luce? Really? <i>Isn't that enough?</i> Why are you such a pathetic loser? How is it that after this entire time you still have about as much self-confidence and identity as a ball of lint? The fact is that up to the last few pages of this series, Lucinda Price is still <u>absolutely nothing</u> without a guy to fawn over, and she sees herself as having no value beyond what that guy thinks of her. I mean her entire stinking identity is wrapped up in what a guy thinks of her, she JUST said it right there! And this is just sad. And makes me want to wring her little neck to be quite honest. "Isn't that enough..." GAWD!!<br><br><b>3.) </b>While we're on the subject of how cray-cray Luce and Daniel's "relationship" is, another thing that really bothered me was the fact that there was absolutely no true feeling or passion between them. <i>Nada</i>. Which is nuts, considering that one of the books was titled <i>"PASSION"</i> and their love for each other is supposedly off the charts. But no-- the heat-factor was somewhere between tepid and 1950's-style frigid. There is one point where Luce is embarrassed to tears just standing in front of Daniel in her underwear. What the crap?! This is the guy you've been madly in love with over and over again for thousands of years, who you're willing to lose everything for, and very well might, you potentially have nine days left to be together-- and you're blushing because he might see you in your knickers?? I'm pretty sure that any normal human being with blood pumping through their veins in the same situation would be getting it on like bunny rabbits, but the only thing we get out of Luce and Daniel are a few totally lame kisses that were about as sexy as a lima bean casserole and dialogue that was so awkward, <i>I</i> felt embarrassed for them. Their relationship was completely artificial and I was not once convinced that they truly loved one another. End of story.<br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-yZiz71W2CuI/UL_bij4C0KI/AAAAAAAAD-Q/t4cOgjnUkH4/s1600/444.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="240" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380353228i/706625.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>4.)</b>There is pretty much no continuity in the writing, or the plot, or the characters. In <i>anything</i>. Seriously. Go back to <i>Fallen</i> where we started out in a reform school in rural Georgia, and I have no idea how we got from Point A to Point B. It's like they aren't even in the same series. Yes Luce and Daniel were slight improvements in this book, but they acted nothing like they have throughout the rest of the books. This makes me think that the author really had no idea where the story was going so she had to fudge everything as she went. Maybe that's a jerky thing of me to say, but that's just how it came across. <br><br><b>5.)</b>LK killed off one of the only likable and semi-intelligent characters in the book. I won't say who, but dude really?! Couldn't you have killed off Luce instead lol.... <i>just kidding</i>. Kind of.<br><br><b>6.)</b>The ASPARTAME.... in diet soda..... was created by GOD..... and it has magical properties to HEAL ANGELS.<br><br>I-- my God, I have no words.<br><br>I swear I'm not making this up.<br><br><b>7.)</b>When you get right down to it, the plot still made absolute ZERO sense. Lucifer, the Creator of Evil, is planning to re-create the Original Fall, so that he can effectively wipe out 7,000 years of human history, and it all boils down to the love between Luce and Daniel. OK, um... <i>what??</i> How, why, and what the hell does this have to do with anything? I'm sorry but <i>I. Just. Didn't. Get. It</i>. I mean at times I thought I was catching on, but to be perfectly honest with you, I could not explain the course of action and how it unfolded or <i>why</i> it unfolded the way it did to save my life, probably because it was <i>EFFING CONFUSING AS HELL</i>. And <i>nothing</i> was ever clearly explained. The whole thing about a "key angel" tipping the scales between Heaven and Hell, the reasoning behind Luce and Daniel's "romance" and how it set everything in motion, just everything was so convoluted and off-the-wall nuts. I don't know, maybe I'm just a total idiot, so please, if you are a semi-intelligent person who actually understood what the hell was going on from Book 1 to Book 4, please leave me a point-by-point explanation in the comments-- I would greatly appreciate it. <br><br><b>8.)</b>I cannot tell you how many times the other supporting characters talk about Luce as though she's freaking Daenerys Targaryen on steroids. And I, of course, just couldn't help but shake my head and laugh, because they're all like, "Oh Luce, you are <i>such</i> a strong person! So tough, so brave!" And I'm thinking, did you <i>see</i> Luce in the last three books? Are we talking about the same person?? Are you guys drunk? She's a total idiot! There is absolutely <i>nothing</i> about her that is strong or brave and if I ever came to be as pathetically attached to an a-hole boyfriend as she is, I would probably go light myself on fire and then jump off a cliff. Luce brave, yeah <i>OK</i> Lauren, nice try. It doesn't matter how many times you have your cast singing praises about Luce being Wonder Woman, you can't take a totally bland and unexceptional character who has "Mary Sue" written all over her and try to make her sound like a Mensa-acing Navy Seal just by having everyone else say that she is. Her actions were not smart or brave, just clueless and sad. <br><br><b>9.)</b>The dialogue. Holy crap, it was <i>painful</i>. Like, I don't know how the book went through to publishing with some of this hokey dialogue. Cheesy is the understatement of the century, it was just that bad. Half the time the (teenage) characters talk like they're straight out of 1842 and the other half is soppy back-and-forths between Luce and Daniel that were so stinking awkward I was <i>cringing</i>. The villain dialogue was equally hilarious, and while it provided me with a few laughs, it did nothing for the rest of the story. <br><br><b>10.)</b> OMG the ending. It was so unbelievable cheesy and sooooo lame and anticlimactic, I don't even know where to begin. But here was what I loved most about it-- remember how I said that the plot was insanely confusing and I had no idea how LK was going to wrap things up? Well get this, because I have to admit it was totally brilliant: GOD Himself comes onto the scene and yells, "<i>ENOUGH!</i>" and all major action stops, and then we get about 25 more pages to quietly explain away any other major complications. I swear to you, I am not making this up, THAT is how the whole series and all its conflicts and convoluted loose ends were neatly tied. Well played, LK, well played. That was quite the crafty move to wrap up this humdinger of a series. <br><br>So, final verdict? Well, believe it or not after all this ranting, it actually wasn't as bad as it could've been. I'm glad I finished the books and got to see where everything ended up, even though I still have no idea how or why anything happened the way it did. There were parts to this book and the series overall that were good, but in the end it just didn't deliver. Entertaining, yes. Good writing with good story and interesting characters, hell to the freaking no.<br><br>Final note, I have to thank<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/36307-skb" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">SKB</a> on Goodreads, who is a total girl genius, for her invaluable tip on reading these books-- and I'm going to pass her secret on to you guys so that you can enjoy them infinitely more as well, because it is flipping brilliant and I love you: Every time you read the word "wings" in this series, replace it with "balls." I promise you, it will have you rolling on the ground in tears laughing.<br><br>You're welcome :)<br><br><b>See more of my book reviews on my YA Book Blog at <a href="http://lcsadventuresinlibraryland.blogspot.com/&gt;%20LC's%20Adventures%20in%20Libraryland&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/b&gt;" rel="nofollow noopener"></a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16939023823611069161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/232771651?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="shady boots" class="user" itemprop="url" name="shady boots" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots">shady boots</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385618120" href="/book/show/15230312-rapture">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=covergasm">covergasm</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=meh-it-was-okay">meh-it-was-okay</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer232771651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14778349222520023399">This review is also available over at <a href='http://wildheartbookblogs.blogspot.com/2012/10/review-rapture-by-lauren-kate.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>my blog.</a><br/><br/>________________________<br/><br/>Actual rating is <b>2.5</b> stars. Yeah, I know right? I expected to give a lower rating.<br/><br/>So. That's it, then. I've finally ended this hot mess of a series.<br/><br/>And . . . surprisingly, I'm satisfied.<br/><br/>I will admit that I actually gave <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9369720.Passion__Fallen___3_' title='Passion (Fallen, #3) by Lauren Kate' rel='nofollow noopener'>Passion</a>, the third book in the series, a three-star rating. It was not as painfully horrible as the first two books, which I both gave one star ratings. But still, even though I did quite like <i>Passion</i>, my hopes</span>
  <span id="freeText14778349222520023399" style="display:none">This review is also available over at <a href="http://wildheartbookblogs.blogspot.com/2012/10/review-rapture-by-lauren-kate.html" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog.</a><br /><br />________________________<br /><br />Actual rating is <b>2.5</b> stars. Yeah, I know right? I expected to give a lower rating.<br /><br />So. That's it, then. I've finally ended this hot mess of a series.<br /><br />And . . . surprisingly, I'm satisfied.<br /><br />I will admit that I actually gave <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9369720.Passion__Fallen___3_" title="Passion (Fallen, #3) by Lauren Kate" rel="nofollow noopener">Passion</a>, the third book in the series, a three-star rating. It was not as painfully horrible as the first two books, which I both gave one star ratings. But still, even though I did quite like <i>Passion</i>, my hopes for the final book in the series were still extremely low. Hell, my hopes for this series had always been low from the very start. I thought that <i>Passion</i> was just a brief ascendance in the series and that <i>Rapture</i> was going to take it right back down the hill again at full speed.<br /><br />I was kind of right, in a way. But it only went downhill for about a few miles and then it just stopped. And very very slightly ascended again.<br /><br />Basically, I'm surprised that I didn't feel disappointment after finishing this final installment. I felt relief, sure, that the series finally ended. But I also felt satisfaction, because I think the series ended in the best way it possibly could. I could think of several even worse endings.<br /><br />So the main reason I'm giving this book a higher rating is because of how it ended. And well . . . I think that really is the only reason. Oh, and maybe Cam is one of the reasons too, even though there's barely enough of him in this book. I will admit now that I love Cam. I really do.<br /><br />Anyways, now onto the fails.<br /><br />As usual the writing is dull and lifeless, and painfully cheesy. You can't go through a single paragraph without seeing the word "love" or things of that nature at least two times. The whole romance in this series is one of the most ridiculous YA romances ever, and I really dislike how the word love is constantly thrown around like it means nothing. You can't fall in love with someone instantly over and over again. I know this is a paranormal romance, but if you're gonna make it take place in the 21st century, you could've at least made it a <i>little</i> bit realistic.<br /><br />Luce during most of the book is pretty much the usual bleak, lost puppy that can't do anything without Daniel that we all know and love to hate. I feel like the author just threw in the few scenes where she did something helpful by herself just to make us believe that she isn't <i>completely</i> helpless, but even those scenes didn't save her. Luce is probably the most pathetic heroine in YA history. Most of the book she's just carried around in Daniel's manly arms, and during most of the action sequences she's always the observer or captive. But I guess since she's human she can't do anything among immortal fallen angels. At least that's realistic.<br /><br />I have nothing to say about Daniel, really. He was just bleh in this book. In the first book he was a grade-A asswipe, in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7740152.Torment__Fallen___2_" title="Torment (Fallen, #2) by Lauren Kate" rel="nofollow noopener">Torment</a> he was super controlling and treated Luce like she was his daughter, and in <i>Passion</i> he was . . . well, I don't know, to be honest. I feel the same way about Daniel as I did when reading <i>Passion</i>. His personality just faded, and I pretty much stopped caring about him entirely.<br /><br />As for the plot, I thought it was very tedious. Most of the time we just see the gang flying around looking for stuff. We meet a few new characters—one of them I actually liked a lot, but Lauren Kate decided to kill them off. Of course. But anyways, something happens nearing the end that made me go all "What the actual eff is going on?" at first and just didn't make any sense at all, but continuing further, I ended up thinking it was a pretty interesting twist. One I actually didn't expect.<br /><br />I was going to give this probably 1.5 stars, or at the very most 2, but the end made me raise it a little higher because I'll admit it was a pretty decent way to end a series. If I had to rate the series as a whole, I would probably rate it about 2 stars. Ish.<br /><br />All in all, this series was a hot mess. It was filled with lows, but it had a few highs as well, and it wrapped up nicely. I don't think this is the worst series I've ever read, but I can't say that it wouldn't be on my top five. If you haven't read the first book, I suggest you avoid it, though.<br /><br />But if you really wanna give it a try, then help yourself. I made it out alive and with barely any bruises or scratches, so maybe it'll be the same for you.<br /><br />I warn you, though, you have to prepare for the worst when starting. Don't come yelling at me if you find yourself losing several of your brain cells.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14778349222520023399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer316261721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2611791367910072599"><b>
  <a href='http://wp.me/p24XSo-Wb' rel='nofollow noopener'> Read full Review at Bewitched Bookworms </a>
</b><br/><br/>I am in awe of this series... If there is any epic love story, then it's the one from Luce and Daniel. Fallen was one of the first books I read after my Twilight Obsession and I love this series ever since. Funny enough, I fell in love with Daniel the minute he flipped Luce off when they first met in Fallen. This series broke me heart so many times, I cried so many times and I swooned so many times. Finally, with Rapture we get closure. We had a wonde</span>
  <span id="freeText2611791367910072599" style="display:none"><b>
  <a href="http://wp.me/p24XSo-Wb" rel="nofollow noopener"> Read full Review at Bewitched Bookworms </a>
</b><br><br>I am in awe of this series... If there is any epic love story, then it's the one from Luce and Daniel. Fallen was one of the first books I read after my Twilight Obsession and I love this series ever since. Funny enough, I fell in love with Daniel the minute he flipped Luce off when they first met in Fallen. This series broke me heart so many times, I cried so many times and I swooned so many times. Finally, with Rapture we get closure. We had a wonderful time together...<br><div></div><br><div>
  <a href="http://wp.me/p24XSo-Wb" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380375645i/730267._SX540_.jpg" alt="" width="491" height="118" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br>This is the most epic love story ever!<br>Yes I mean it!<br>Epic!<br>True Love!<br>True Soul Mates!<br><br> The End <br><div>Last books are always hard. There are so many loose questions that now finally need to come to an end so that the reader gets closure, so that we can finish this series and feel satisfied. Lauren Kate gave us all this - she went beyond from what I first expected when I picked Fallen up a few years ago. The mythology behind Daniel's and Luce's love story was so incredible and epically heartbreaking. During every book throughout the series we learned more and more, new layers and mysteries were revelaed and each left us breathless with the enormity of this epic love story.</div><br><br><br><br>..this story finally came to an end, some things I suspected, some surprised me. However, this was a fitting end to an beautifully woven love story that is beyond everything I read before ...<br><br>I'm glad and sad its over! This was an emotional roller coaster and my heart needed Luce and Daniel story to come to and end, I was ready....<br><br>Dear Mrs. Kate:<br>Please,please please I want, no - I need a Cam spin off! <br>Thank you very much! <br>Yours,<br>Danny <br></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer345273140" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10428425615504193661">NEVER AGAIN WILL I HAVE TO READ ANOTHER BOOK IN THIS SERIES! I'm sorry, i'm just so excited that it's over. I could rant and rave about all the plot holes and "plot surprises" (i.e the surprises that you could easily guess 1/4 of the way through the book) but i won't. I will leave it at this- For the sake of your sanity, don't read this series. In fact, don't read ANY books by her.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer169404106" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17197942415458400544">This was quite and ending to a wonderful series, and I have to say that Rapture really tugged at my heart. I didn't think I would have this reaction. I didn't think the end of the series would affect me this much, but it has. I am saddened to know that Rapture is the final book *actually crying here.* And no one will understand this more than my fellow readers *sniff sniff.* I really hate saying goodbye to characters that I have grown to love over the years. We have shared some good times, and b</span>
  <span id="freeText17197942415458400544" style="display:none">This was quite and ending to a wonderful series, and I have to say that Rapture really tugged at my heart. I didn't think I would have this reaction. I didn't think the end of the series would affect me this much, but it has. I am saddened to know that Rapture is the final book *actually crying here.* And no one will understand this more than my fellow readers *sniff sniff.* I really hate saying goodbye to characters that I have grown to love over the years. We have shared some good times, and bad. We have fallen in love, over and over again, for a millennia and we have challenged evil, for the sake of the world. This story really was something special *sighs.* <br /><br />I really don't think I should give an outline as to what happens in the story. Let me just say that you will all get the answers you need and more. So much goes down it really is hard to divulge without spoiling it, so trust me, if you are a fan of the Fallen Series, Rapture will not disappoint. The only thing that made me sad the most was the ending just a little, only because I didn't want to say goodbye. Not to Luce and Daniel, or Arianne and Roland, or Annabelle and especially not to Cam, my sweet but oh so devilish Cam :( Oh how I wish that Lauren Kate writes his story. Cam, has so much to tell and it sort of felt like the best was yet to come with him. And, it was a scene with Cam and Luce, right at the end that made me start to cry. I had to share it here. "He drew her close, and for a moment, she thought he was going to kiss her. Her heart pounded as his lips bypassed hers and came to a stop, whispering in her ear: 'Don't let him flip you off next time.'" I just lost it here when Cam said this to Luce :( He may have chosen the side of Lucifer, but he still knew what it meant to love and lose it. I love you Cam!<br /><br />Ok, on that note, while I wipe the tears away, I am signing off and saying goodbye to a wonderful series that will forever be in my heart, and made me believe that no matter what, I'll can and always will choose love! Beautiful!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17197942415458400544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_365985331" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/365985331" />
    <a title="Lighthearted" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1132923-lighthearted"><img alt="Lighthearted" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372874200p2/1132923.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/365985331?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lighthearted" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lighthearted" href="/user/show/1132923-lighthearted">Lighthearted</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1132923-lighthearted?shelf=supernatural-fiction">supernatural-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1132923-lighthearted?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1132923-lighthearted?shelf=fallen-angels-fiction">fallen-angels-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1132923-lighthearted?shelf=star-crossed-lovers-fiction">star-crossed-lovers-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer365985331&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer365985331" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5753723374066340078">What a disappointment. The first book in the series, Fallen, snared me with its gorgeous cover and its intriguing premise. The ending of that book should have made me realize that Kate really didn’t have the story worked out. Torment and Passion added very little to the story and, aside of the insight into Roland and Arriane’s histories, Fallen in Love annoyed me.<br/><br/>Rapture quite simply ticked me off. The promise of an interesting story has always been there but Kate hasn’t delivered since the firs</span>
  <span id="freeText5753723374066340078" style="display:none">What a disappointment. The first book in the series, Fallen, snared me with its gorgeous cover and its intriguing premise. The ending of that book should have made me realize that Kate really didn’t have the story worked out. Torment and Passion added very little to the story and, aside of the insight into Roland and Arriane’s histories, Fallen in Love annoyed me.<br /><br />Rapture quite simply ticked me off. The promise of an interesting story has always been there but Kate hasn’t delivered since the first book in the series. Fallen angels living amongst us on earth, star-crossed lovers, a mysterious curse–I wanted to like this series. Despite the fact that I felt that Kate was just making details up as she went along, without ensuring that they tied into the story as a whole, the premise and a few of the characters wouldn’t let me give up on the series. Here’s a short list of what ticked me off about this book (believe me, it could have been longer).<br /><br />Unanswered questions. We still don’t know why the fire started in Fallen, the one that killed Trevor and set Luce on her path to meet Daniel. This is a big deal. My guess is that Kate originally meant the Announcers to be something other than what they were; when she decided it was better to make them useful rather than malevolent, she either forgot that she needed an alternate explanation for Trevor’s death, or she assumed we no longer cared. Wrong.<br /><br />Flawed mythology. The Fallen are angels who either sided with Lucifer right off the bat or didn’t take a side, right? What makes the Outcasts more lowly than the other undecided angels? Oh, and really, Luce is going to give God conditions for making a decision??? That doesn’t even work with mere mortals–why would it work on a being who can wipe out one’s very existence?<br /><br />Flawed story. God never says that love is forbidden–so why the hell do Luce and Daniel have to make a decision between God and Lucifer all about them? This is the most annoying flaw of the storyline.<br /><br />Kate really can’t keep her story straight. Previously in the series, we were given the impression that the Fallen didn’t have the option to return to Heaven, yet in Rapture, we’re given the impression that this happens from time to time. Daniel can’t enter a sanctuary submerged by the ocean but several of the Fallen can enter a sanctuary buried by boulders? God loses her temper before the Roll Call is even finished, so some of the angels didn’t even get a chance to vote? But they worked their way up the list–or down, I don’t remember? If they were working their way down from the highest, Luce was only third in line (yes she’s an archangel) and she didn’t vote so God must have lost her temper right after Gabbe, sending most of the angelic host earthward–but that couldn’t have been the order because Daniel was sixth on the list, I think, and we know what he said. If for some reason, God was working her way up from the lowest to the highest–which doesn’t seem likely given that the rank seems to be the heavenly way–and Daniel cast his non-vote, angering God, then a handful of archangels would have been kicked out without voting–yet Daniel acts as if several angels were affected. None of this makes sense.<br /><br />Where did that come from? Luce was initially attracted to Cam in Fallen, then she hated him for the filler books, and now suddenly she cares about him? And Lucifer was her first love? WTH? I mean, I got the Luce/Lucifer love connection right away when I started reading Rapture but shouldn’t there have been some buildup from the beginning of the series? Instead Kate set it up to look like Cam may have been Luce’s first love. There’s misdirection and then there’s just poor plotting. I suspect that Kate originally meant for Cam to be Lucifer but maybe not. Either way, I wish that she had sprinkled more clues about Luce’s relationships with both characters throughout the series.<br /><br />That’s predictable. It was pretty easy to see where Kate was going in Rapture. Luce is really an archangel, she was in love with Lucifer before Daniel etc. The only surprise in the book was that there was no big battle between the Fallen and Lucifer–just a lame conversation between Luce and Lucifer and a ridiculous scene featuring God, Luce, Daniel and Lucifer.<br /><br />That’s convenient. Despite the fact that he’s an angel and a historian, Daniel’s memory can’t be trusted. I actually bought the bit about the trauma of the Fall but I simply don’t accept the rest of the conveniently forgotten history.<br /><br />Luce loves Lucifer, Luce loves Daniel, Luce loves??? Don’t just tell me that Luce loved Lucifer until he got a bit full of himself, then she spotted Daniel and fell in love with him–make me believe it. As it reads now, Luce seems to fall in love based on appearances only–Kate spends a lot of time telling us that Luce and Daniel are in love with each other but the only thing we actually see is them looking into each other’s eyes, kissing, and declaring their love for each other. Is their love based on anything other than physical attraction? They’ve never had much time together in any lifetime to figure that out.<br /><br />Luce and Daniel are the two most self-absorbed, selfish protagonists EVER. Again, God never said that they couldn’t love one another so I don’t understand why a choice between God and Lucifer was answered with “we choose each other”. What I see here are two smug individuals, so caught up in their newly discovered “love” for each other that they want to make sure everyone knows how in love they are. Aside of Lucifer, I doubt that anyone cared. I would have liked God to say something like, “Well, that’s just fine and dandy that you love each other but that wasn’t the question. The question was Do you want to stay in heaven–under my protection, by the way,–or do you want to make camp with Lucifer? Who looks like he’s about to curse you, by the way? Even assuming God had forced the issue, shouldn’t Luce be concerned for her family and friends? They will simply lose her. For their choice, Luce and Daniel will die now and be reincarnated later as mortals. God makes no promises that they will ever find each other again, and, as they’ve never spent much time together in any lifetime, who really knows if their love will last once there’s no curse to ramp up the excitement.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5753723374066340078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review266943738">

<span id="freeTextContainer17296579433550371046">This series was not my favorite at all. I totally loved the first book, but the second and third sequel took me forever to finish. But I think "Rapture" was able to redeem itself. I admit that I was totally lost with some recap scenes, but I think the story was good. Although I never expected the ending to be good. <br/><br/>I totally loved Cam. I was really hoping he could atleast have a happy ending for himself, but I was wrong. Coz' until the end, Cam's love for Luce was sad and wasn't returned. I was </span>
  <span id="freeText17296579433550371046" style="display:none">This series was not my favorite at all. I totally loved the first book, but the second and third sequel took me forever to finish. But I think "Rapture" was able to redeem itself. I admit that I was totally lost with some recap scenes, but I think the story was good. Although I never expected the ending to be good. <br /><br />I totally loved Cam. I was really hoping he could atleast have a happy ending for himself, but I was wrong. Coz' until the end, Cam's love for Luce was sad and wasn't returned. I was really thinking that the first love of Luce will be Cam. But I was totally wrong. AGAIN. So you see, this book has lot of twist and turns. I think this sequel is a worth to read after all.<br /></span>

<div id="review_368941510" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/368941510" />
    <a title="Charissa Sophia de la Rosa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7108558-charissa-sophia-de-la-rosa"><img alt="Charissa Sophia de la Rosa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398029499p2/7108558.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/368941510?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charissa Sophia de la Rosa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charissa Sophia de la Rosa" href="/user/show/7108558-charissa-sophia-de-la-rosa">Charissa Sophia de la Rosa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780375897191" href="/book/show/12848043-rapture">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">YA readers who wants to read an example of true love!, Hopeless Romantics like me. *sighs*</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7108558-charissa-sophia-de-la-rosa?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7108558-charissa-sophia-de-la-rosa?shelf=inspiring-books">inspiring-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7108558-charissa-sophia-de-la-rosa?shelf=books-that-made-me-cry-sob">books-that-made-me-cry-sob</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7108558-charissa-sophia-de-la-rosa?shelf=books-with-a-great-ending">books-with-a-great-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7108558-charissa-sophia-de-la-rosa?shelf=cliffhanger-endings">cliffhanger-endings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7108558-charissa-sophia-de-la-rosa?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7108558-charissa-sophia-de-la-rosa?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7108558-charissa-sophia-de-la-rosa?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7108558-charissa-sophia-de-la-rosa?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7108558-charissa-sophia-de-la-rosa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer368941510" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer620568464709924198">As the last installment for the Fallen series, Lauren Kate did a truly spectacular grand finale for one of the best YA book series. It made me feel a lot of emotions like happiness, sadness and a mixture of both. It made me laugh, anxious and cry. Now, that's the true definition of an unforgettable story.<br/><br/> <br/><b> What I Love: </b> <br/><br/>[_] The plot. Ever since I had read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6487308.Fallen__Fallen___1_' title='Fallen (Fallen, #1) by Lauren Kate' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fallen</a>, I know there's something worth reading in it. Have you ever read a YA book where there are two lovers and the girl keeps on dying at t</span>
  <span id="freeText620568464709924198" style="display:none">As the last installment for the Fallen series, Lauren Kate did a truly spectacular grand finale for one of the best YA book series. It made me feel a lot of emotions like happiness, sadness and a mixture of both. It made me laugh, anxious and cry. Now, that's the true definition of an unforgettable story.<br /><br /> <br /><b> What I Love: </b> <br /><br />[_] The plot. Ever since I had read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6487308.Fallen__Fallen___1_" title="Fallen (Fallen, #1) by Lauren Kate" rel="nofollow noopener">Fallen</a>, I know there's something worth reading in it. Have you ever read a YA book where there are two lovers and the girl keeps on dying at the age of seventeen? And despite of the 'dying' part, they still love one another so much the guy is willing to wait for more thousand years and still love the girl for a thousand more even if there's a chance that they will never end up together? (Ok, I got that from my favorite song "A Thousand Years" by Christina Perri.)<br /><br />Now, that's what I call a unique and beautiful plot every girl (especially hopeless romantics like me) would truly want to read. An everlasting true love- a love that never dies and will stay bind together no matter what happens and succeeds in the end. <br /><br />[_]The ending! It should be given emphasis for how brilliant, astounding, amazing and wonderful it is! The ending is truly unpredictable and gives a loud BOOM (or explosion) to the whole plot of the story. It is one of the <b> BEST </b> endings I've ever read that made me feel so happy and sad at the same time. And it also made me bawl my eyes out for crying over Luce and Daniel. D":<br /> <br />[_] The characters! Sure, Luce can be Bella-like sometimes but I still adore her in some ways. <br /><br />And Daniel, goodness! Don't even get me started on Daniel! He is the ideal guy every girl will die for! I've never seen such loyalty and devotion he showed to Luce and take note: He's willing to wait and suffer for her just to show how much he truly loves her! Ahh! That is truly romantic! I wish there's a real Daniel still present in this world! <br /><br />Arriane: tsk tsk, at first, I really like her but <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12588363.Fallen_in_Love__Fallen___3_5_" title="Fallen in Love (Fallen, #3.5) by Lauren Kate" rel="nofollow noopener">Fallen in Love</a>, it is revealed that she is actually a lesbian and her lover, who is a demon, already died of blood loss  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, I don't like her that much anymore. <br /><br />Gabbe: I already like her since the first book. I know there's more to her than good looks. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ And I grieve so much when she died protecting Luce and Daniel. R.I.P. Gabbe. :'(  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />Molly: At first (by Luce's description in Fallen), I dislike her but after reading that scene <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ where she, together with Gabbe protected Luce and Daniel from the deadly starshots and getting killed in the process  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, I like her. She's one of the least persons I'll ever think that will do such a thing! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ And I'm pretty sure Gabbe and Molly knew what the price is when they saved Luce and Daniel.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />Cam: I like him and it is a pity he didn't end up with anyone. :'( <br /><br />Roland: I like him too! And here I thought he and Arriane will make a good couple! His love life is truly tragic and even if he's a demon, he's a really good person and doesn't deserve such a thing (I'm talking about his valentines day in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12588363.Fallen_in_Love__Fallen___3_5_" title="Fallen in Love (Fallen, #3.5) by Lauren Kate" rel="nofollow noopener">Fallen in Love</a>). <br /><br />The characters are really likable and everyone can relate to them. <br /><br />[_] Writing style. I love Lauren Kate's writing style! The words flow freely like the river peacefully flowing to the waterfalls. I also love how the scenes harmonized together.<br /><br />[_] Cover! The cover is very catchy just like the other three installments and like the other three, Luce was shown. Truly artistic. <br /><br /><br /><b> What I dislike: </b> <br /><br />[_] Lucinda is kind of a Mary-Sue. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Lucinda Price is actually an angel favored by God and the third archangel. Ok, that's alright but that's not the reason why I called her a Mary Sue. The only thing I couldn't understand is that why Lucinda is actually a lover of Lucifer. Seriously? Does it sound good to you? I mean, come on! I didn't <i> ever </i> think Lucifer can actually know what love is! And also according to this book, Lucifer invented Love. Oh great.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But since it's fiction and a fantasy YA novel, anything's possible. So yeah, that's my only problem but now that I'm thinking of it, it did add a spice on the story. But I still dislike it. Sorry. :/<br /> <br />[_] There are some things that up till to the fourth book, Lauren Kate didn't clear up and will possibly stay vague and a mystery to all of us. <br /><br />[_] The ending! I dislike how cliffhanger-y the ending is! It is a major case that made me want to bang my head countless of times! <br /><br />(Oh, that reminds me what Rick Riordan did on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9520360.The_Son_of_Neptune__Heroes_of_Olympus___2_" title="The Son of Neptune (Heroes of Olympus, #2) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Son of Neptune</a> that I needed o wait a <b> WHOLE </b> year just to know what happened next! Argh! **bangs head* But at least, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9520360.The_Son_of_Neptune__Heroes_of_Olympus___2_" title="The Son of Neptune (Heroes of Olympus, #2) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Son of Neptune</a> still has a sequel while <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12716010.Rapture__Fallen___4_" title="Rapture (Fallen, #4) by Lauren Kate" rel="nofollow noopener">Rapture</a> is already the end which up till now, by the way, something I can't accept.)<br /><br />Yes, I know that it is really good and that's why I put it to the things I love but what Lauren Kate did to the ending is unforgivable! Waaahhh! Lauren Kate should really make a sequel to this series! <br /><br />I need more Luce and Daniel moments in here! Like how did Luce and Daniel <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ now as ordinary human beings  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> develop and end up together? Will the newly born Luce and Daniel still recognize Arriane, Roland, Cam, Shelby and Miles when they meet? Or will they ever meet them again? What'll happen when they died? Are they going to Heaven and still be together? Argh! *bangs head* I. NEED. MORE! <br /><br /><br /><b> Conclusion: </b> <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12716010.Rapture__Fallen___4_" title="Rapture (Fallen, #4) by Lauren Kate" rel="nofollow noopener">Rapture</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2905297.Lauren_Kate" title="Lauren Kate" rel="nofollow noopener">Lauren Kate</a> is a really great book with a great plot and a spectacular ending that will always stay not only in my mind but also to the other YA readers who'll never forget the strong and everlasting true love Luce and Daniel shared. And the ending is truly breathless for it gives you this feeling that they're finally allowed to be together up to the end of their lives. <br /><br />Even if Luce is kind of a Mary-Sue and there are still some questions that are left unanswered and will stay as a mystery, I'm giving Rapture by Lauren Kate five stars. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="620568464709924198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_184768186" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/184768186" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5738587-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586448699p2/5738587.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/184768186?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/5738587-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer184768186" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12098583588277109962">So, we have the conclusion of Lauren Kate's Fallen series.<br/><br/>I have to say: as much as I trash this series, it does hold a place in my heart. It's like that annoying sibling you love, but want to punch so damn bad.<br/><br/>I stared out LOVING this series so much, I shoved it onto my friends (sorry guys). They didn't like it as much as I did, and all I had to say was "Whaaaat?"<br/><br/>The second book, I still liked, but not as much as I remember loving the first. It took me a couple tries to get into.<br/><br/>Third is where </span>
  <span id="freeText12098583588277109962" style="display:none">So, we have the conclusion of Lauren Kate's Fallen series.<br /><br />I have to say: as much as I trash this series, it does hold a place in my heart. It's like that annoying sibling you love, but want to punch so damn bad.<br /><br />I stared out LOVING this series so much, I shoved it onto my friends (sorry guys). They didn't like it as much as I did, and all I had to say was "Whaaaat?"<br /><br />The second book, I still liked, but not as much as I remember loving the first. It took me a couple tries to get into.<br /><br />Third is where I started to see why so many people hated this series. It was between <i>Torment</i> and <i>Passion</i> where I started to get into the mythology of angels and demons, and saw the terrible flaw in Kate's mythology.<br /><br />I have to say, though, <i>Rapture</i> was a teeny bit better than <i>Passion</i>!<br /><br />Okay, so now that Luce and Daniel are back in the present, they have to stop Lucifer from once again falling from Heaven and sending time back to before the fall. In order to do this, the team must split up into three groups to find the three ancient relics. In doing so, they will find the site of the Fall and will be able to stop Lucifer.<br /><br />Short summary, but that is the main point of the final novel. Pretty interesting, no?<br /><br />Well, unfortunately that brings our main problem. Remember those three groups? Well, it turns out that Daniel and Luce are in a group of their own (shocker). You know what that means~!<br /><br />Boring, sappy romantic time!!! Woo!<br /><br />Oh, wait, that's bad.<br /><br />Luce and Daniel make the most insipid couple ever! They are so boring together, I felt myself wanting to just outright skip most of the scenes (I didn't, though).<br /><br />They are alone together for about a third of the book. Ugh.<br /><br />My second complaint: Cameron. Cam is not a bad character, not at all. Cam is the best piece of work Kate has come up with. It's the LACK of him I have a problem with! He wasn't really even there until the last third, and even then, he rarely spoke. <br /><br />It's like Kate realized that most of the people reading this series are doing so, so we can see Cam, therefore took him out of most of the series. Makes no sense considering he was a crucial part of the first book.<br /><br />I'm pretty sure that was my ultimate downfall with the series--when I realized Cam was barely in it.<br /><br />Now, the mythology still bugged me, a lot, but I will not go into detail on it. I did enough of that in my review of <i>Passion</i> and I don't want to get too repetitive. <br /><br />What I will say is that her change of the people in the archangels really, really bothered me. *twitch*<br /><br />It seemed that Kate tried to make Luce "tough" in this novel...It didn't work.<br /><br />There was one scene where Cam was in trouble. They made it seem like she was the one to save him, when all she did was, well...get up and nearly got hit with a starshot. It was Roland and Cam who really solved all this.<br /><br />Yes, Cam saved HIMSELF before Luce could do anything.<br /><br /><i>"You're so brave."</i>~The single most stupid thing I have EVER heard Cam say...<br /><br />And one other thing...when did Cam and Luce become BFFs? She HATED him through the first three books, and all of a sudden she couldn't stand to lose him?<br /><br />Girl has issues.<br /><br />The "big reveal" was also pretty dumb. I won't spoil it for you (surprising, right), but I will say that it made me scratch my head and roll my eyes.<br /><br />Oh, and God is female in this book. Right. So THAT'S why us women bleed through our woman areas ever month and go through painful childbirth. Because God is a WOMAN!<br /><br />Spiteful, I tell you.<br /><br />The ending was sweet, though. Like, the very ending. By the ending, I mean the last two chapters and the epilogue.<br /><br />Just one question...WHERE'S CAM?!<br /><br />Honestly, the way the ending was left, I could see a spin-off for Cam. I hope that happens.<br /><br />Then again, he may end up like...*shudder*...Daniel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12098583588277109962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

However, the books do read easily.<br/>I can't say that I'm sorry to see this series end. I'm glad I bought them as a bargain, and that I've sold them again for the same price.<br/>Nope, I will not read number 5 from Cam's point of view, nor will I read the short stories. I'm done with the series :p</span>

<div id="review_452472292" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/452472292" />
    <a title="Katy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4572741-katy"><img alt="Katy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365039295p2/4572741.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/452472292?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katy" href="/user/show/4572741-katy">Katy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780307706553" href="/book/show/15797430-rapture">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer452472292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14816844614875126502">THAT was the series was about?!?! All the bloodshed, all the heartache, and THAT was the cause of it all?!?! I'm truly flabbergasted! And then to say, <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>["Perhaps I didn't want it after all." <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> What. The. Heck?!?! It's just with all the trouble everyone went through, I was just expecting it to be some apocalyptic battle at the end, and it ended up being an anticlimactic um, agreement? Don't get me wrong, I'm glad that <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[basically nothing happened <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoi</a></span></span>
  <span id="freeText14816844614875126502" style="display:none">THAT was the series was about?!?! All the bloodshed, all the heartache, and THAT was the cause of it all?!?! I'm truly flabbergasted! And then to say, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["Perhaps I didn't want it after all." <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> What. The. Heck?!?! It's just with all the trouble everyone went through, I was just expecting it to be some apocalyptic battle at the end, and it ended up being an anticlimactic um, agreement? Don't get me wrong, I'm glad that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[basically nothing happened <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but at the same time, I'm disappointed because the series built up to that deciding moment, and I was left wondering, "That's it?!?"<br /><br />Deep breaths. I hope the rest doesn't come off as a rant, because that's not my intention - just the first part. :P<br /><br /><b>
  <u>I remember liking the first book,</u>
</b> but I think I read the next two books just so I can find out what happens next.<br /><br />First of all, wow, I don't remember the books being <b>
  <u>so overwritten.</u>
</b> I like descriptions to allow me to picture the scenes in my head, but the writing was <b>
  <u>so bogged down with details</u>
</b> on surroundings and each little thing about someone's appearance or action, and then it goes an extra few miles to tell us how the character feels. Okay, I get the point. I really just wanted to find out what happened next. But I think I summarize everything and put it in an novella, and the reader wouldn't miss a thing. This is not to diss on Kate's writing because I know she put a lot of work into it, but I just don't think her effort helped her in this book.<br /><br />And I <b>
  <u>really struggled for the majority of this book</u>
</b> because I couldn't figure out which "side" the Scales were on and the Outcasts, and how they all fit into the whole "Fall" story. It's not that I didn't understand the story. I just didn't get what was the point of those little episodes and how they helped lead to the end.<br /><br />What's more, the thing that was great about the previous three books was the reader had a chance to learn more about Luce's past (why I like reading time travel books). However, in this book, the majority of the <b>
  <u>memories were short glimpses.</u>
</b> Nothing in depth except the original life, which we don't see until near the end.<br /><br />Sadly, I <b>
  <u>didn't connect with the characters</u>
</b> in this book. Daniel wasn't very swoony in this book, and Lucinda made me want to shake her more than once. I really liked Gaby and Cam, but they weren't even in a good part of this book. And I know Luce and Cam had a "past," and Dee kept alluding to there was more to their relationships (not necessarily romantic), but I'm still confused on that. Even when Cam leans in to whisper in her ear, Luce thought he wanted to kiss her. What was up with them?<br /><br />Having said that, I didn't totally hate the book. <b>
  <u>I liked that Luce was finally - yes FINALLY - able to find out the real story behind that.</u>
</b> And aside from the reason of the fall, I thought <b>
  <u>who Luce really was and how she and Daniel first fell in love was really interesting.</u>
</b> I just thought the whole "feelings" description was <b>
  <u>a bit over the top and even a bit cheesy,</u>
</b> but tone it down a bit, and it <b>
  <u>could be a really good romantic story.</u>
</b> Like I said earlier, the reason for all the bloodshed was just kind of lame, and the way it ended was like, "Wow, all those people died just for that, and you're just going to just shrug and say, 'Oh well,' and it's over?" Still, like I said, it wasn't to the point where I hated the story.<br /><br />Just a little additional note. Kate made Plano, Texas sound like a country hick town in the boonies, but it's actually a rather sophisticated suburb of Dallas. And the weather is actually dry heat compared to Austin or Houston's mugginess. Which is why I'm surprised to find out Kate went there for high school.<br /><br />Also, about the reader. Like I said, the book was a bit overwritten, and the feelings descriptions were a bit over the top and cheesy. However, the lady who read the book greatly added to that "oh come on" thought I had as I went through the book. Maybe it was a talent that she was able to dramatize the words, but the writing itself did enough of that. Just not a great combination, in my opinion, when I already thought it was melodramtic enough.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14816844614875126502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EorWeU4RsVe/zKQZ2l2b4vbonnwcRsMtF2tpOLcc6ngorL+r9U94PxjnEHgtqJE9ILd5tNLLTUpMFS+Jel8Y4g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RkQdMFDUeX5imxTZVX5szbxyvhy3/hxA7T2qR54M3zx8YnTi64qwFsWwoLiii2YSai1Z1Hlzkie2Q+z2U08tpg==')})
  }

And his freshest Hell is high school, where Lilith, the girl he can’t stop loving, is serving out a punishment for his crimes.\n\nCam made a bet with Lucifer: he has fifteen days to convince the only girl who really matters to him to love him again. If he succeeds, Lilith will be allowed back into the world, and they can live their lives together. But if he fails…there’s a special place in Hell just for him.\n\nTick-tock.\n\nSpread your wings and cry as bad boy dark angel Cam finally reveals his anguished heart in the epic new FALLEN novel,
